28.   The water supply works and equipment are in poor state of repair due to low
quality of materials used for construction, poor initial construction, and many-
years absence of maintenance. The quality of water supplied is unsatisfactory as
a result of inadequate treatment and lack of disinfection. Also, supply is
intermittent, for several hours per day or even for some days during the week.
29.   A new source of water for Dien Vong treatment plant will be the recently
completed Cao Van dam about 4.5 km upstream from Dien Vong treatment plant.  The
dam has been designed to be constructed in two phases of 60,000 m3/d each. The
dam design and quality of construction have been inspected by an expert in June
1995; he will continue such inspections annually for the next three years. First
inspection report is available in the project file.
Sewerage and drainage
30.   Sewerage and drainage services in the component area are managed by the
Halong City Environment and Sanitation Company (ESC) and Cam Pha Town Sanitation
Company (SC), both administrative enterprises reporting to the city and town
People's Committee, respectively, through their Urban Departments. In addition



56                     ANNEX  1
to sewerage and drainage, the companies manage street cleaning, solid waste
collection and disposal, maintain public toilets, cemeteries, public parks and
street lights. To supplement their resources they also undertake minor
construction works and develop and operate rental housing. The companies are
headed by a Director assisted by two Vice Directors, one in charge of sanitation
and environment and the other in charge of construction, including operation of
rental housing, and maintenance of street lights. In 1995 the Halong and Cam Pha
companies had 190 and 170 employees, respectively.
31.   In 1995, about 82% of households had their own latrine and 10% used public
latrines while 8% had no access to toilet facilities. There is a shift towards
construction of pour flush latrines with septic tanks; it can be expected that
a great number of other types will be converted in very near future.
32.   Halong and Cam Pha are served by about 53 km of combined sewers.  It
consists of open channels with minor length of pipework, designed as storm water
drainage. The channels are normally short and discharge directly in the Halong
Bay. Due to lack of maintenance a number of channels are completely blocked with
solid waste, sand and gravel, some of the channel outlets and some length of
pipework have collapsed, all resulting in surface flow or flooding even during
average storms. In addition, during low tides the normally submerged drainage
outfalls are exposed with untreated wastewater flowing slowly on mud flats from
where various sea food for domestic consumption Ls collected.
Nightsoil and septage disposal
33.   The latrines' pits and vaults are typically made smaller than recommended
and need emptying about four times per year. The septic tanks were constructed
largely during last two years and have not yet been cleaned. The emptying of pits
and vaults is normally done by farmers free of charge. On request it is also
pumped out by the Sanitation Companies which also service public toilets. Sullage
is typically disposed of directly into drainage channels or into septic tanks.
Solid waste management
34.   The solid waste services are managed by the Halong and Cam Pha Environment
and Sanitation Companies. Daily generation of solid waste in both communities is
estimated at about 150 t/d (375 m3/d) with a considerable part being organic,
while recyclable materials such as paper, plastic, metal and glass form a very
small part. The solid waste collected from households, hospitals and industries
is disposed of at two waste dumps serving the Halong City and the Cam Pha town.
Inappropriate disposal of solid waste causes malfunctioning of the drainage
system, generates breeding of insects and rodents, leads to general environmental
degradation of the communities and contributes to pollution of Halong Bay.
DANANG COMPONENT
Population
35.   The third largest city in Vietnam and one of the four with provincial



57                     ANNEX  1
status, Danang city is situated on the coast in central Vietnam about midway
between Hanoi and HCMC. It has a major deep water sea port and good access to
communication network through the National Highway #1 and Trans Vietnam railway.
About 52% of population is working primarily in manufacturing, such as textile,
and consumption goods, and services sectors such as commerce, transportation,
tourism and government. A considerable proportion of the labor force, though, is
in temporary or part-time employment. The city's master plan proposes development
of tourist resorts along the coast, commercial centers and industrial export
zones which in aggregate would contribute to increase of current city's GDP from
US$380 per capita to US$760 per capita in 2000. Beside receiving substantial
share of the national investment in improving infrastructure, the master plan
assumes a steady flow of private capital in industry and tourism.
36.   The city is divided into three districts and further subdivided in 28
wards. It covers an area of 43,200 ha, excluding the airport and Son Tra
Mountain. The airport is zoned for national defence purposes and Son Tra Mountain
with its steep slopes is not suitable for urban development; both are, therefore,
excluded from the area under control of the city administration. Sector-wise, the
city administration controls drainage and waste management while water supply is
controlled by the provincial government.
37.   The Danang city population of 450,000 in 1995 is expected to grow to about
500,000 in 2000 due to natural increase and migration. It is planned that after
2000 the city administrative area will about double and include about eight
neighboring communes; aggregate population is projected to reach about 680,000
in 2005 and 765,000 in 2010. The average household of 5.9 persons in 1995 is
planned to reduce to less than 5 after 2005.
Water supply
38.   Water supply services are managed by the Danang Water Supply Company (WSC),
a provincial business enterprise, reporting to the Provincial PC through its
Construction Bureau. It has 230 permanent employees headed by the Director and
assisted by a Chief Accountant and a Vice-Director in charge of the
Administration Department and the Technical Department, respectively
39.   The 1995 production and distribution capacity of the WSC system was 40,000
m3/d and the daily average production was 52,000 m3/d or 270 lcd, including about
33% of non-revenue water. Water services were provided through 21, 000 connections
to commerce, industry and 191,000 population (47% of total). About 93% of all
connections were residential, using about 54% of water supplied and 7% were
commercial and industrial using 13%. Remaining 33% was non-revenue water.
Private shallow wells, providing about 12,500 m3/d and serving 40% of population,
are inadequate and polluted and should be considered a temporary source. The
projected daily average water demand and production capacity assuming 25% of NRW
are shown in Table A-1.4.
40.   The principal water source for Danang is the Cau Do River.  Two separate
intakes on that river, located about 10 km south of the city center provide raw
water for treatment plants at Cam Le adjacent to the intakes and San Bay near the



58                     ANNEX  1
airport. Minor supplies are taken from streams on Son Tra peninsula and treated
in Son Tra two treatment plants.  Cam Le and San Bay plants use conventional
treatment technology and have capacity of 20,000 m3/d each. Son Tra plants with
a combined capacity of 5,000 m3/d use only filtration and chlorination and
provide supply in the Son Tra peninsula only. The distribution network consists
of a number of smaller reservoirs with the total volume of 15,000 m3, several
boosting pumping stations, and about 130 km of mains with diameters varying from
100-900 mm. The tertiary distribution network is practically non-existent. Its
functions have been replaced by extremely long individual connections (spaghetti
connections) which draw water directly from mains.

Sewerage and drainaqe
41.   Sewerage  and  drainage  services  are  managed  by  the  Danang  Urban
Environmental Company (URENCO), an administrative enterprise, reporting to the
city's PC through its Construction Bureau. In 1995 URENCO maintained 37 km of
sewers which operated as combined sewerage system for stormwater and wastewater.
The system, which serves only about 30% of the urban area, is overloaded and in
poor state of repair; it discharges into city's lakes and rivers without any
treatment and the level of maintenance and cleaning is low. The Construction
Bureau is preparing improvement and expansion of the system.
42.   In 1995, about 87% of households in the area had their own latrine and the
remainder had no toilet facilities. There is an observed shift towards
construction of pour flush latrines with septic tanks and it can be expected that
a great number of pit latrines will be converted in very near future.
Nightsoil and septage disposal
43.   It is estimated that Danang population generates daily about 10,000 t of



59                    ANNEX  1
septage. Of this quantity, the Danang URENCO and private contractors collect
about 150 t/d and dispose it at Dai La landfill. The remaining is used as
fertilizer by owners or collected free of charge by farmers.
Solid waste management
44.   The solid waste services and street sweeping are also managed by URENCO.
In 1995 about 350 ton of solid waste of about 450 ton generated was collected and
disposed of daily at the Dai La open dump. The rest is burned or buried at source
or scattered illegally. In addition, URENCO sweeps about 57 km of streets.

60                   ANNEX  2
VIETNAM
WATER SUPPLY PROJECT
Prolect description
Proiect location and content
1.    The project,  located  in Hanoi,  Haiphong,  Quang Ninh and Danang,  will
improve (a) water supply facilities, and (b) operation and maintenance through
provision of various equipment and vehicles to operating agencies. The consulting
and advisory services will assist in (a) implementing the project, (b) training
of administrative, technical and managerial staff of the agencies, and (c)
preparing proposed follow up project. Detailed description of project components
and consulting services is as follows:
HANOI COMPONENT
2.    The component will include construction of:  (a) production wells and two
treatment  plants,  (b)  primary,  secondary  and  tertiary  distribution  network
including large water meters, and (c) new residential connections and replacement
of existing connections made of GS pipe. The consulting services will include,
construction management, advisory assistance, and training.
Production wells
3.    Augmentation  of  water  source  will  include:  (a)  development  of  new
wellfields at Cao Dinh in north-west and at Nam Du in south-east of the city to
provide 30,000 m3/d of additional water from each field; in each wellfield this
will comprise construction of 9 new production wells with diameters of 600 mm and
average depth of 65 m, equipped with submersible pumps and 3-5 km of transmission
mains with diameters varying from 200-800 mm for conveying raw water from the
wellfields to treatment plants; and (b) construction of about 4 new wells in the
existing wellfields to compensate for decrease in production of operating wells
and 5 km of transmission mains with diameters varying from 400-600 mm.
4.    On the basis of ground water flow modelling both wellfields are located
along Red River on sites with high infiltration potential estimated at 80,000
m3/d in Cao Dinh and 120,000 m3/d in Nam Du, i.e. in both instances several times
higher than the proposed extraction.
Treatment plants
5.    The Cao Dinh and Nam Du treatment plants each with capacity of 30,000 m3/d
will include (i) aeration chamber to remove high concentration of iron and
manganese, (ii) contact basin to facilitate precipitation of oxidized iron, (iii)
rapid sand filtration, to remove iron and manganese flocs, (iv) disinfection by
liquid chlorine,  (v) clear water reservoir,  and  (vi) pumping station.   Major
units of treatment plants are shown in the Table A-2.1



61                   ANNEX  2

Network, metering and connections
6.    The network will be improved by (a) 21 km of primary mains with diameters
varying from 300-1000 mm, (b) 80 km of secondary network with diameters varying
from 100-250 mm, (c) 250 km of tertiary network with diameters less than 100 mm,
and (d) 60,000 new service connections. Metering within the network will be
strengthened by installing 30 large meters with diameters varying from 400-600
mm. Galvanized steel (GS) pipe used for construction of about 30,000 existing
connections will be replaced by pipe made of more suitable materials.
Construction management and institutional support'
7.    Construction  management  will  support  the  Hanoi  WBC  in  day-to-day
supervision of construction. The consultant assistance will include verifying the
compliance with specification for works and goods, supervising the adherence to
the construction schedule, testing and commissioning the completed works,
approving manuals for operation and maintenance, advising on training of staff
identified to operate completed facilities, preparing progress reports and other
documents required for carrying out the works.
8.    Institutional support will be focused on facilitating commercialization of
the WBC, on supporting the project implementation by carrying out various
studies, on training to ensure proper operation and maintenance of facilities and
on preparing the follow-up project.   Support to commercialization will include:
(a) upgrading of accounts receivable accounting module, (b) improved customer
relations,   including  associated  field  work   (mapping,   customer  register,
disconnection-reconnection, etc.), and (c) development of O&M guidelines to form
a basis for establishing adequate budget allocations and evaluation of company
performance.
1 Finnida-financed except for construction management.



62                   ANNEX  2
9.    Supporting studies will include (a) monitoring of the groundwater and land
subsidence, evaluation of data and plan of action for future use of groundwater
and various investigations, evaluation of data and implementation of actions
aimed at protection of the groundwater against surface and sub-surface pollution;
and (b) non-revenue water identification pilot study to identify, quantify,
monitor, and evaluate components of non-revenue water. It will be located in two
target areas in Hanoi city, facing relatively similar water accessibility, but
having different socio-economic characteristics. The latter study is planned to
be carried out in 1998.
10.   Training will  focus on accounting  staff,  to ensure  that modified and
improved  accounting  modules  are  implemented2.  All  trained  staff  will  be
evaluated through suitable testing. The follow-up water supply project will
expand water production and distribution capacities. Terms of reference for
engineering and other studies to prepare the project will be completed by the
Hanoi WBC in March 1999.
11.   The construction management is estimated at 570 person-months, supporting
studies and training at 230 person-months and preparation of follow-up project at
50 person-months. Outline terms of reference for the studies and training
programs are available in the project file.
Land recruirement and resettlement
12.   The component will not involve resettlement of population but will require
land acquisition of about 8.6 ha for construction of two WTPs, 3.4 ha for
production wells, and 3.2 ha for raw water mains and access roads or 15.2 ha of
paddy fields and fish ponds. About 13.2 ha will be required temporarily for
construction of distribution networks. The production wells and treatment plants
are located outside the built up urban center.
HAIPHONG COMPONENT
13.   The component includes:  (a) construction of raw water pipeline from the
existing intake at Quan Vinh to An Duong treatment plant and rehabilitation of
raw water pumping station, (b) reconstruction of An Duong treatment plant and
expansion of its capacity, (c) construction of primary distribution pipeline
serving Haiphong city center and Quan Toan township including balancing reservoir
and  booster  pumping  station,   (d)  improvement  of  secondary  and  tertiary
distribution network in 17 phuongs, including water connections, and (e)
provision of various equipment, materials and vehicles required for operation and
maintenance. The consulting services will include construction management,
various advisory assistance, and training.
2 Hanoi Water Supply and Sanitation Program financed by Finnida includes extensive training

Raw water pumping and transmission main
14.   At Quan Vinh intake, raw water is pumped from the An Kim Hai irrigation
channel into concrete boxed conduit (1.2m xl.4m) through which it gravitates to
An Duong treatment plant. The conduit is in a bad state of repair and will be
rehabilitated during the next expansion phase. In the meantime it will be
replaced by a new raw water pipeline with 1.0 m diameter,  4.0 km long and a
capacity of 100,000 m3/d, which will be laid along the country road from the
intake to the An Duong plant. The intake pumping station will be repaired,
provided with new pumps and motors, including electrical installation. The
existing conduit will be retired upon commissioning of new transmission main and
retained as possible stand-by.
Treatment plant
15.   The An Duong plant uses conventional treatment process including raw water
pre-sedimentation (30,000 m3), pumping station (1,200 m3/h), mixing chambers,
sedimentation tanks (1,152 m2), rapid sand filters (450 m2), chlorination, water
reservoir (9,400 m3), and pumping station (1,200 m3/h) . The rehabilitation and
upgrading of the plant will use sedimentation tanks for expansion of filters,
improve mixing, flocculation, filter washing, and instrumentation, expand
reservoir, renovate various equipment and increase the capacity from 60,000 to
100,000 m3/d. Key units of renovated treatment plant are shown in Table A-2.2.

Support facilities

fitters, water meter mechanics, water meter readers, i.e. essentially trade

QUANG NINH COMPONENT
25.   The  component  will  include  (a)  rehabilitation  of  deep  wells,  (b)
construction of raw water transmission main from the intake to treatment plant,
and rehabilitation of two raw water pumping stations, (c) rehabilitation of two
treatment plants, (d) renovation of existing and construction of new transmission
and primary distribution mains, (e) upgrading and expansion of secondary and
tertiary distribution network, (f) repair and renewal of booster pumping
stations, (g) repair of existing and construction of new water reservoirs, (h)
rehabilitation of existing and construction of new residential connection
including meters, and (i) provision of various equipment, materials and vehicles
required for operation and maintenance of provided facilities.   The consulting
services will include construction management, advisory assistance, and training.
Production wells
26.   Ten wells with major potential capacity located in Bai Chay, Hong Gai and
Cam Pha will be rehabilitated; this will include replacement of well head,
screens, electrical installation, pumps and repair of structures and of
associated pipework. The rehabilitation is expected to increase total capacity of
deep wells from the current 20,000 m3/d to 32,000 m3/d.   After completion of
treatment plants the use of groundwater will be discontinued and facilities
maintained as a stand-by.
Raw water pumping and transmission mains
27.   Transmission main 5,7 km long and diameter 900 mm will convey raw water
from Cao Van dam to the treatment plant; along the pipeline will be provided a
rudimentary access road. Boosting pumping station, which will use residual
pressure in transmission main will be located at the end of transmission main to
lift raw water into the treatment plant. Booster station will include pumps,
motors, associated piping, electrical installation, instrumentation and surge



66                   ANNEX  2
protection. The transmission main and boosting station will have a capacity of
60,000 m3/d, boosting will have a head of about 40 m.
28.   The old intake at Dong Ho as well as raw water transmission main will
require only minor repairs.   Structures of existing pumping station will be
repaired and painted, and the station equipped with new pumps, motors, associated
piping, electrical installation, instrumentation and surge protection. Intake,
pumping station, and transmission main will have a capacity of 20,000 m3/d,
pumping head will be 40 m.
Treatment plants
29.   Dien  Vong  treatment  plant  (serving  Hong  Gai  and  Cam  Pha)  will  be
substantially rehabilitated to restore its initial capacity of 60,000 m3/d;
structures of the plant and administrative building will be repaired, surfaces
renovated and painted, major part of equipment, some pipework and all electrical
installation,   instrumentation  and  controls  will  be  replaced.   Similarly,
structures of treated water reservoir will be repaired and pumps, electrical
installations and controls in treated water pumping station, including metering
and surge protection will be replaced. Capacity of treated water pumping station
will be about 60,000 m3/d and pumping head about 80 m.
30.   Dong Ho treatment plant with design capacity of 20,000 m3/d (serving Bai
Chay) will be renovated; structures of treatment plant, and treated water
reservoir will be repaired, surfaces renovated, major part of equipment, some
pipework and all electrical installation, instrumentation and controls will be
replaced. Key units of both treatment plants are shown in Table A-2.3.
Network, reservoirs, boosting, metering and connections
31.   Improvement of the network will include  (a) reconditioning of 78 km of
transmission mains with diameters 800-200 mm, and construction of 38 km of new
primary distribution mains with diameters 400-200 mm, (b) construction of 64 km
of new secondary distribution network with diameters 250-100 mm, and of 113 km of
new tertiary network with diameters 90-50 mm,  (c)4 rehabilitation of existing
12,000 and construction of about 20,000 new residential connections including
meters, and (d) repair of six existing (11,800 m3) and construction of three new
(4,500 m3) water reservoirs. Major and secondary booster stations will be
substantially renewed, pumps, piping, electrical installations and controls will
be replaced and structures repaired and stations provided with fence.
Support facilities
32.   Facilities will include provision of various equipment for maintenance of
network such as various vehicles with loading equipment, leak detection equipment
and spare parts, and improvement of store and workshop. Office equipment will
include provision of computers, printers, copier and telefax.

facilities are properly operated and maintained in accordance with standard
public utilities practices. The operational staff which require training are
categories such as treatment plant operators, pump attendants, pipe fitters,
water meter mechanics, water meter readers, i.e. essentially trade categories
which are not formatted within the standard educational stream. All trained staff
will be evaluated through suitable testing. The follow-up water supply project
will expand water production and distribution capacities. Terms of reference for
engineering and other studies to prepare the project will be completed by the
Quang Ninh WSC in March 1999.
38.   The construction management is estimated at 535 person-months,  supporting
studies and training at 220 person-months and preparation of follow-up project at
40 person-months. Draft terms of reference for the studies and training programs
are available in the project file.
Land recquirement and resettlement
39.   The  component  will  require  land  acquisition  of  1.6  ha  of  degraded
mountainous area and cultivation land for construction of a 5.7 km of raw water
main from Cao Van dam to Dien Vong WTP. Construction of treated water reservoirs
will require about 1.1 ha of plantation and government land. About 465 structures
are located on top of the existing water mains, and demolition of parts of these
structures will be required during rehabilitation works. All other works will be
carried out in the existing premises and along the roads. About 64 ha of road
area will be temporarily required for the distribution networks.
40.   The Cao Van dam, now completed with Government financing will provide water
for Halong water supply system. Construction of the dam involved resettlement of
some population in the reservoir area and borrow pit. In accordance with
Government regulations full compensation has been paid at the start of
construction a few years ago. Resettlement of last group, consisting of about 12
families, is being currently processed.
DANANG COMPONENT
41.   The Danang component will include construction of: (a) raw water intake;
(b) raw water transmission main; (c) treatment plant, treated water reservoir and
sludge lagoon at Cam Dai; (d) treated water transmission main to Cam Le; (e)
access roads; (f) primary and secondary distribution mains and bulk meters; (g)
tertiary network and new connections. Various equipment, materials and vehicles
required for operation and maintenance will also be provided.   The consulting



69                   ANNEX  2
services will include construction management, various advisory assistance and
training.
Intake, transmission main, salinity weir
42.   A new raw water intake will be located at Yen Ne on the northern bank of
Cau Do River below the confluence of the Tuy Loan and Yen Rivers.   The intake
structure will be of reinforced concrete in wingwall configuration with an apron
at the same level as the river bed. It will be constructed for the ultimate
capacity of 240,000 m3/d and the installed capacity of 120,000 m3/d. From the
intake raw water will be pumped into the treatment plant through a transmission
main (1.0 km, diameter 1100 mm, pumping head 40 m) provided with a surge
protection.6
Treatment plant
43.   A treatment plant with a capacity of 120,000 m3/d and reservoir (20,000 m3)
will be constructed at Cam Dai. The location of the plant at Cam Dai with
elevation of between 35-45 m will allow gravity supply with minimum pressure in
the network of 10 m. The treatment technology and type of treatment units will be
subject to selection on basis of performance bids. The bidding documents will
identify site, critical elevations of structures, soil and foundation conditions,
quality of raw water and required quality of treated water and will specify
required performance of the plant.
Network, metering and connections
44.   The network will be improved by construction of: (a) transmission main from
the treatment plant to Cam Le (2.0 km, 1200 mm diameter); (b) primary and
secondary distribution mains (57 km, with diameters varying from 1200-150 mm),
including master meters; (c) tertiary network (206 km, with diameters varying
from 100-50 mm) with about 40,000 metered individual connections and repair of
about 12,000 residential service connections. Metering within the network will be
strengthened by installing large meters.
Support equipment
45.   Support will include provision of various equipment for maintenance of
network, various vehicles with loading equipment, and spare parts.
Construction management and institutional support7
46.   Construction  management  will  support  the  Danang  WSC  in  day-to-day
supervision of construction. The consultant assistance will include verifying the
compliance with specification for works and goods, supervising the adherence to
6 The need for protection of the intake against salinity intrusions and technical aspects of such protection
will be determined by separate studies to be carried out within the component's technical assistance.
I AusAID-financed except for construction management.



70                   ANNEX  2
the construction schedule, testing and commissioning the completed works,
approving manuals for operation and maintenance, advising on training of staff
identified to operate completed facilities, preparing progress reports and other
documents required for carrying out the works.
47.   Institutional support will be focused on facilitating commercialization of
the WSC, on supporting the project implementation by carrying out various
studies, on training to ensure proper operation and maintenance of facilities and
on preparing the follow-up project.   Support to commercialization will include:
(a) upgrading of accounts receivable accounting module, (b) improved customer
relations,   including  associated  field  work   (mapping,   customer  register,
disconnection-reconnection, etc.), and (c) development of O&M guidelines to form
a basis for establishing adequate budget allocations and evaluation of company
performance.
48.   Supporting studies will include monitoring of the water quality in the
source, evaluation of data and plan of action for future use of that source and
identification of actions aimed at protection of the source against pollution,
and  assessment  of  factors  contributing  to  observed  internal  and  external
corrosion of pipes.
49.   Training with key emphasis on skill development will include local training
of trade categories and non-professional staff; greater external exposure of
professional staff will be provided through study tours, language training, and
participation in national and regional professional conferences
50.   Training will focus on (a) accounting staff, to ensure that modified and
improved accounting modules are implemented; and (b) operational staff, to ensure
that new facilities are properly operated and maintained in accordance with
standard public utilities practices. The operational staff which required
training are categories such as treatment plant operators, pump attendants, pipe
fitters, water meter mechanics, water meter readers, i.e. essentially trade
categories which are not formatted within the standard educational stream. All
trained staff will be evaluated through suitable testing.   The follow-up water
supply project will expand water production and distribution capacities. Terms of
reference for engineering and other studies to prepare the project will be
completed by the Danang WSC in March 1999.
51.   The construction management is estimated at 705 person-months,  supporting
studies and training at 290 person-months and preparation of follow-up project at
50 person-months. Draft terms of reference for the studies and training programs
are available in the project file.
Land requirement and resettlement
52.   The component will require 20.3 ha of land in total comprising of 12 ha of
eucalyptus plantation (which belong to government) for construction of Cam Dai
WTP, water reservoir and an access road; 4 ha of rice field for the sludge
lagoon; 1.35 ha of rice field for Yen Ne intake; and 3 ha of rice field and
inhabited land for construction of 2.2 km access road from Yen Ne intake to Cam
Le WTP. The latter will also involve resettlement of about 98 households.



71                    ANNEX  2
Construction of a raw water main from Yen Ne to Cam Dai WTP will require
temporary land (rice field and cultivation) of about 10 ha, as will laying of
distribution network along 263 km of roads.

105                         ANNEX 7
VIETNAM
WATER SUPPLY PROJECT
Environmental impact
Requirements
1.    The Ministry of Science, Technology, and Environment (MOSTE) administers the
Environmental Protection Law (EPL-1993) through its Department of Natural Resources
and Environment. The Department is also responsible for recommendations on policy,
rules, regulations, and guidelines, including environmental quality standards, and
reviewing and approving environmental impact assessments  (EIA) .  The People's
Committee (PC), assisted by provincial environmental department (DOSTE) is
responsible for implementing the EPL, including monitoring and enforcement.
2.    EIAs are required for development projects under the EPL.  Large projects,
including those with an investment cost of more than US$20 million, must submit an
EIA to MOSTE for approval. For smaller projects, it is submitted to the DOSTE.
3.    The project's land acquisition and resettlement would affect a limited number
of people; most of the other negative impacts are temporary, which would be
mitigated through good planning and construction practices. According to World Bank
(WB) guidelines, the proposed project is classified as a category "B" project, which
requires an environmental management plan (EMP) satisfactory to the Bank.
Proiect Description
4.    The project involves rehabilitation and expansion of water supply facilities
in Hanoi, Haiphong, Quang Ninh, and Danang and will be implemented by the various
cities' water supply companies (WSCs) from 1997-2001. Details are in Annex 2.
EIA Studies
5.    The EIAs were carried out as part of the feasibility studies and the reports
are available in the project file.  They concluded the project will positively
affect the living standards and health conditions of the population. Rehabilitation
of the existing facilities will decrease the level of non-revenue water while
expansion of treatment plants and transmission and distribution lines will improve
the quality of water provided and increase the amount of water supply, service
levels and revenues.
6.    The project's negative impacts would only be temporary, minor and reversible
which can be mitigated through proper policy and project planning, public relations,
and good construction and supervision practices. The engineering preparation of the
project was guided by the requirement to reduce land acquisition and resettlement
as much as possible.   Therefore,  the project will require only limited land
acquisition, relocation of population and demolition of houses.
7.    Serious  negative  impacts  during  site  clearing,   rehabilitation,  and



106                         ANNEX 7
construction of the project facilities are not expected. Most of the WTPs, intakes,
and other facilities are located far from residential areas. The mountainous area
in Quang Ninh where raw water mains will be laid and the hill in Danang where the
WTP will be constructed are degraded and serious impacts on ecology are not
expected. Construction of the distribution networks will be carried out along the
roads  and  sidewalks.    While  serious  adverse  impacts  on  residents  are not
anticipated, consultations with the affected population will be carried out prior
to construction; in addition, at the design phase, efforts will be made to further
reduce land requirements.  The standard measures to mitigate the impacts during
construction, including provision of adequate and safe water during the interruption
the water services, will be required and included in the bidding and contract
documents.
8.    During operation, the WTPs would generate treatment sludge and improved water
supply would contribute to increasing volumes of wastewater. The sludge would be
disposed of in sludge retention lagoons in WTPs and when dried, disposed of in
controlled landfills. Increases in wastewater volumes would have no significant
impact on the current status; in addition, the sanitation project being prepared in
the four cities would improve current conditions.
9.    Serious impacts on water resources are not anticipated since the abstraction
and pumping rates are relatively small compared to the annual average flow in the
water resources.   Monitoring of land subsidence and possible contamination of
groundwater in Hanoi is important, and the program established and carried out by
the city will be continued.   For Quang Ninh, the safety of Cao Van dam will be
improved and monitored. Trees and large shrubs in the reservoir were removed before
filling, to improve the water quality. A program to protect the relevant watersheds,
water quality at the intakes and in the water supply system against pollution will
be developed and implemented (see Annex 2).
Environmental Management Plans
10.   In line with the EPL, the project's EIAs were cleared by MOSTE.  Also, the
World Bank requires that, based on the EIAs, the WSCs would prepare an environmental
management plan (EMP) and a resettlement action plan (RAP) for each component.
Accordingly, the WB received information on MOSTE's clearance and EMPs for each
component before appraisal and found them satisfactory.
11.   The EMPs summarize the mitigation measures proposed for the construction and
operation of the components and are available in the project file. The measures are
summarized below and those mitigating the adverse impacts due to land acquisition
and resettlement are summarized in the next section.
12.   During construction, the contractors will be required to carry out the works
according to international standards, including consulting with residents; providing
safe and adequate temporary paths for residents and businesses; providing adequate
safety to the public and workers; implementing effective measures to reduce erosion,
dust, and noise due to construction equipment; providing limited transport and
construction along the main roads in urban areas during rush hours and in the
residential areas at night; appropriately disposing of surplus soil and construction



107                        ANNEX 7
materials; and providing adequate water supply by other means when the system is
interrupted.   These requirements are included in the bidding documents and the
contractors will be liable for all damages caused by non-compliance.
13.   Prior to starting construction, the WSCs will inform the public and residents
about the project through various means/media and EIA reports will be made available
for public review. The public relation program will be carried out on a continuous
basis.  During construction, WSCs assisted by consultants, will cooperate with
affected residents and take all measures needed to minimize the impacts to the
residents and public.
14.   The increase in the quantity of piped water produced would substitute for
existing non-piped sources leading to minimal net increase in the quantity of
wastewater generated. Pollution control is planned through a separate sanitation
project now under preparation.   To ensure adequate protection of water quality
against pollution at the intakes and in the water supply systems, a monitoring
program and various investigations will be conducted in each component; terms of
references for the studies are available in the project file. Training will also
be provided in the project to ensure effective operation and maintenance of the
water supply facilities.
15.   Specific programs for Hanoi, Quang Ninh and Danang systems will also be
carried out under the project's technical assistance. This includes monitoring
groundwater and land subsidence in Hanoi; enhancing the safety of Cao Van dam in
Quang Ninh; and conducting a comprehensive study of Cau Do River in Danang.
Technical assistance for Hanoi will be financed by the Finnish Government while for
Quang Ninh and Danang, it will be provided by the Danish and the Australian
Governments, respectively.
Land Acquisition and Compensation
16.   A total of about 36 ha will be acquired of which over one quarter are under
the responsibility of government agencies. Most of the remaining hectares are rice
fields; about 30 houses will be removed for the construction of an access road in
Danang. The land acquisition process will be carried out in line with the national
laws and appropriate compensation will be paid to the affected families.  Land
requirements for the project components are given in Annex 2 and summarized in Table
A-7.1.
17.   The government policy on land acquisition and compensation was reviewed during
appraisal and found to be acceptable in principle.   The Land Law (1993), and
implementation directives issued by the provincial PCs stipulate land categories,
compensation procedures, and price ceilings for loss of land and property (houses,
other structures, trees, crops, etc). During the process, representatives of the
affected families will be included on the compensation committees and will have the
means to redress grievances.
18.   The land acquisition process normally takes about 2-3 months and is summarized
as follows:



108                         ANNEX 7
* The WSC, consulting with the local government (communes), will carry out a
field survey identifying the type of land use, number of people affected,
extent of the impacts, and the estimated amount of compensation;
* The WSC will submit the survey with the request for land acquisition and a
proposal for compensation to the Land Service Department (LSD);
* After receiving the request, LSD will carry out a field inspection,
confirming the type of land categories, number of the affected population and
the level of compensation, and submit a recommendation to the provincial PC;
* The PC will establish a compensation committee, consisting of
representatives from the WSC, concerned agencies, local PC, and affected
population to evaluate the adequacy of the compensation and consult/negotiate
with the affected groups. The committee will submit the results to the PC for
approval;
* If agreement is reached, the WSC will compensate the affected people
directly and the right to use the land will be transferred to the WSC, so
construction can begin;
* If the affected families are not satisfied with the decision, they can
submit their proposals to the  provincial PC for consideration within 15
days. The PC will respond to the proposal within 1 month;
* Any land acquisition of more than 5 ha must be approved by the Prime
Minister's Office.
Implementation of the EMPs/RAPs
19.   During appraisal, the compensation policy for each component was reviewed in
the light of the World Bank policy on resettlement and the WSCs agreed to proceed
as follows:
* The proposed EMPs/RAPs presented in the project implementation plans (PIPs)
will be timely and strictly implemented and results will be periodically
reported to IDA;
* During the design stage for the water mains and distribution networks,
efforts will be made to minimize: (a) the impacts on houses, buildings and
graves; (b) land requirements; and (c) excavation of large quantities of
soil. The aim will also be to lay the pipes along the side of roads where
impacts on households and businesses are less intrusive. Where the damages is
more serious, pipes will be laid under the roads;
* Bidding documents will include specific mitigation measures required during
construction, and the contractors will be liable for damages caused by non-
compliance;
* EIAs will be made available for public review; consultation with the public
and residents will be carried out through various means/media on a continuous
basis;
* During construction, the WSC, assisted by consultants, will supervise the
work and inform residents and the public about all aspects of the project;
* WSC will be responsible for preparing and implementing the RAP, consulting
with the affected groups, and carrying out the land acquisition process
according to national laws. Efforts will be made to ensure that the affected
population are not worse off after the project, and that their incomes and
living standards are recovered or improved. The process will be completed at



109                         ANNEX 7
least one month before construction begins;
* The affected assets will be compensated at their replacement value and
depreciation will not be considered during the calculation;
* Representatives of the affected population will be included as members of
the compensation committee to ensure their concerns are adequately addressed
during the acquisition process and that the level of compensation is
acceptable;
* WSC will conduct a detailed survey on the affected population, including
living standards, level of income, other social conditions, opinions about
the project component, and the level of compensation and other assistance.
Farmers loosing more than 25% of their total holdings will be identified, and
a program to provide assistance will be developed so their economic
conditions can be reconstituted. Results of the survey, including the level
of compensation and payment schedule as proposed by WSC and, if possible, as
agreed with the affected people, will be submitted to IDA for review;
* Along with the above, WSC will proceed with the formal process and
incorporate IDA comments; the compensation plan approved by the Government
will then be submitted to IDA;
* Land acquisition will be carried out in line with the project
implementation schedule and will be completed at least one month before
construction begins;
Particular Actions
* In Hanoi, a program to protect groundwater and the water supply system
against pollution will be prepared and implemented, and the existing program
to monitor groundwater and land subsidence will be continued;
* In Haiphong, a program to protect water quality at Quan Vinh intake and the
water supply system against pollution will be prepared and implemented;
* In Quang Ninh, a program to strengthen safety at the Cao Van dam and to
protect water quality at the intakes and in the water supply system against
pollution will be prepared and implemented;
* In Danang, details on the land acquisition of the access road from Yen Ne
intake to the existing WTP at Cam Le will be prepared and submitted to IDA
for review. Also, a program to study Cao Do River and protect water quality
at the intakes and in the water supply system against pollution will be
prepared and implemented.
During appraisal, the WSCs confirmed the above agreements.
Government Approval of the EIAs and Compliance
20.   The EIA reports for the Hanoi, Haiphong, Quang Ninh and Danang components were
submitted to MOSTE and the environmental clearances were obtained between August and
October 1996.  Each implementing agency (WSC) declared its willingness to comply
with all conditions as required by MOSTE; compliance will be monitored by the
DOSTEs. The MOSTE and DOSTE capacity, although still limited, is being gradually
upgraded by the Government, helped by various bilateral grants.

Project supervision plan
IDA Supervision Input into Key Activities
1.          The staff input indicated in the table below is in addition to regular
supervision needs at headquarters to review progress reports, procurement actions,
correspondence, etc., which is estimated at 4 staff weeks during FY97, 12 staff
weeks during FY9B through FY01 and 8 staff weeks in FY02. The Bank Resident Mission
assistance in coordinating the four components is estimated at 5 weeks annually from
FY97-02. Accordingly, the total IDA supervision input is estimated at 79 staff
weeks, of which 20 staff weeks would be at the headquarters, 34 staff weeks in the
field, and 25 staff weeks would be at the Resident Mission.

112                         ANNEX 8
Borrower's Contribution to Supervision
2.          Overall coordination of the project would be the responsibility of
Hanoi Water Business Company (WBC). This would include inter alia (i) providing
guidance on timing and form of reporting implementation progress; (ii) arranging
meetings with the government, provinces and water companies during mission's field
visits; (iii) chairing mission's opening and wrap-up meetings; (iv) ensuring timely
information to IDA; and (v) proposing satisfactory resolution of any unexpected
issue occurring during implementation. The WBC would be assisted by the staff of
Hanoi Resident Mission.
3.          The following reports on implementation progress would be submitted to
IDA: semiannually: (a) reports on implementation status, including monitoring of EMP
and RAP; annually: (b) annual updated financial projections of water companies; (c)
audited financial statements of water companies and Special Accounts for the credit
including a separate opinion on Statement of Expenditures; and other: (d) evaluation
report on project implementation and any report required on various subjects.
Outline of semi-annual status report
4.    The semi-annual status report will be prepared by each WSC. The report should
comprise a descriptive part and appendices; the descriptive part should not exceed
twenty pages and should cover the following items:
(a)   General  description of the project.  A  concise summary of project
objectives, description cities' components, financing, initial and
latest estimated costs, initial and latest schedule, key data of credit
and project agreements and of various amendments;
(b)   Project overview,  physical accomplishment.  Status of implementation
progress for each component of the project, procurement, information
on inspection of manufacturing, input of supervising consultant;
monitoring of EMP and RAP, compliance during the reported period;
(c)   Procurement status. List of awarded contracts with dates of award, start
and completion of contract, allowed time extensions, and variations,
contract amounts in various currencies and status of disbursement for
contracts, projected and actual disbursement S-curve for the total cost;
(d)   Institutional status. Progress of institutional improvements in water
companies, performance of advisers and achievements in staff training;
(e)   Problems affecting implementation. Description of problems and proposed
or taken actions.
5.    Appendices will list personnel provided by the provinces and water companies,
by the consultants and by contractors, key meetings, important visits on site,
photographs, location plans of the project showing planned and achieved progress and
monitoring indicators.
6.    The report will include key monitoring indicators shown in Annex 11.



113                         ANNEX 8
Outline of the evaluation report on project implementation
7.    The evaluation report will be prepared by each WSC.  It should not exceed ten
pages and the performance judgments and analyses should cover the following specific
aspects:
(a)   Project  objectives.   A concise  statement  and evaluation of major
objectives as presented in the SAR, including any changes made during
implementation.    The  evaluation  will  assess  the  clarity  of  the
objectives, their realism, and whether they are important for the
country and sector.
(b)   Achievement of project objectives.   An assessment of the project's
success (substantial, partial, negligible) in achieving its major
objectives - e.g. sector policy improvements, financial objectives,
institutional development, physical objectives, other social objectives,
environmental objectives, and public sector management and private
sector development.
(c)   Implementation record and major factors affecting the project.   An
analysis of the factors that affect implementation.   The factors are
divided into those not generally subject to government or provinces
control, those subject to government and provinces control, and those
subject to water companies control.
(d)   IDA  performance.     An  assessment  of  IDA's  performance   (highly
satisfactory, satisfactory, deficient) in project identification,
preparation assistance, appraisal, and supervision.
(e)   Water companies and provinces performance.   An assessment of the
performance of involved water companies and provinces (highly
satisfactory, satisfactory, deficient) in preparing, implementing, and
operating the project.
(f)   Assessment of outcome.   A rating of outcome  (highly satisfactory,
satisfactory, unsatisfactory, or highly unsatisfactory) based primarily
on how well the project achieved its objectives and how sustainable it
is likely to be.
(g)   Future operation.   A description and assessment of the plan for the
project's future operation, including understanding the measures to
maximize the project benefits, and the indicators for monitoring and
evaluating future operations.
(h)   Key lessons learned.  A discussion of the most significant positive and
negative lessons learned from the project's implementation, showing how
they are reflected in the arrangements for its future operations. This
section also identifies those lessons most relevant to similar ongoing
and future projects in this sector in Vietnam.
8.    WSCs will submit the evaluation report to IDA after completing the project and
in time stipulated in the Project Agreement.

VIETNAM
WATER SUPPLY PROJECT
Assumptions for financial projections
1.    The financial statement projections are in current Vietnamese Dong (VND)
Figures for 1994 and 1995 are actual. Local inflation rate of 9% p.a. has been added
for 1996, 7* for 1997, 6% for 1998 to 1999, and 5% from 2000 to the end of the
projection period in 2004. The VND exchange rate for the projection period was set
at VND 11,000 equals US$1.00, and VND 2,100 equals French Francs FFr 1.00.
HANOI COMPONENT
Income statement
2.    Revenues:  Water revenues  have been projected to increase  in line with
estimated increased water supply and annual increases of water tariffs. Water
revenues include a 10% surcharge for sewerage. Water supply is projected to increase
with additional production (30% increase between 1996 and 2001); NRW is projected
to be 66% in 1996, reducing to 50% in 2000, and to reduce by 1% p.a. thereafter.
Average water supply and sewerage tariffs are assumed to increase by 12% p.a. from
1996 to 2001, and by 20% thereafter.
3.    Operational costs: Staff costs: Include wages, bonuses and other benefits for
WBC staff. A 4% annual increase in constant prices has been added to pay levels.
Other costs: Projected expenses are increased in proportion to additional production
capacity. Depreciation: The calculation of 5.65% p.a. has been made on the weighted
average of all fixed assets in operation.
Balance sheet
4.    Fixed assets: Include network, wells, treatment plants (including land), with
the addition of plant and equipment when new assets are placed in service. In 1995,
a valuation of the assets was prepared and used to adjust the value in the balance
sheet. Accounts receivable: Based on past experience, these have been assumed to
reduce from 46 days' sales in 1996 to 42 days' in 2004. Inventories: These have been
assumed to increase in proportion to additional fixed assets in service. Accounts
payable: Historical figures have been projected to increase in line with operating
expenses.
Source and application of funds
5.    Capital contributions:  Actual and projected  contributions by FINNIDA to
support the WBC and the project with trainers and advisors; an equity contribution
towards the project by the Provincial PC of VND 68 billion; additions consist of
equity contributions by the Government equal to the amount of interest during
construction included in the cost of the project Loans: The IDA US$32.5 million
(VND 357.6 billion) credit is assumed to be on-lent to the WBC by the Government
over 20 years, with a five year grace period, at an interest rate of 6.5% p.a. A
loan from France of FFr 7.5 million to assist with metering and billing/collections



127                         ANNEX 10
in a pilot area of Hanoi is assumed over 20 years, with a five year grace period,
at an interest rate of 2.8% p.a.  An additional loan to help fund the follow-up
water supply project on the same terms and conditions as the first loan is assumed
to commence in 2004.
6.    Interest during construction: Capitalized interest charged at 6.5% p.a. on the
on-lent IDA (ITF) credit from 1997 through 2001 for the first project, and from 2002
to 2005 for the follow-up second project.

HAIPHONG COMPONENT
Income statement
7.    Revenues: Water revenues have  been projected  to increase  in line with
estimated increased water sales and annual increases of water tariffs. Water supplv
is projected to increase following the expansion of the Cau Nguyet treatment plant;
NRW is projected to be 67% in 1996, reducing to 50t in 2004. Average water tariffs
are assumed to increase in current prices by 15% from 1996 to 2001, and by 20%
thereafter.
8.    Operational costs: Staff costs: Include wages, bonuses and other benefits for
WBC staff. A 4% annual increase in constant prices has been added to pay levels.
Other costs: Projected expenses are increased in proportion to additional production
capacity. Depreciation: The calculation of 5.65% p.a. has been made on the weighted
average of all fixed assets in operation.
Balance sheet
9.    Fixed assets: Include network, treatment plants (including land), with the
addition of plant and equipment when new assets are placed in service, and are
revalued at annual projected inflation rates. Accounts receivable: Based on past
experience, these have been assumed to equal 42 days' sales. Inventories: These have
been assumed to increase in proportion to additional fixed assets in service.
Accounts payable: Historical figures have been projected to increase in line with
operational expenses.
Source and application of funds
10.   Capital contributions:  Actual  and projected contributions by FINNIDA to
support the WSC and the project with trainers and advisors; other additions consist
of equity contributions by the Government equal to the amount of interest during
construction included in the cost of the project. Loans: The IDA US$19.6 million
(VND 216.3 billion) credit is assumed to be on-lent to the WSC by the Government

over 20 years, with a five year grace period, at an interest rate of 6.5% p.a. A
second loan to help fund the follow-up water supply project on the same terms and
conditions as the first loan is assumed to commence in 2004.
11.   Interest during construction: Capitalized interest charged at 6.5% p.a. on the
on-lent IDA (ITF) credit from 1997 through 2001 for the first project, and from 2002
to 2005 for the second project.

QUANG NINH COMPONENT
Income statement
12.   Revenues: Water revenues have been projected  to increase  in line with
estimated increased water billed and annual increases of water tariffs. Water billed
is projected to increase with reduction of NRW which is projected to be 58% in 1996,
reducing to 40% in 2004. Average water tariff is assumed to increase in current
prices by 10% from 1997 to 2001, and by 20% from 2002 to 2004.
13.   Operational costs: Staff costs: Include wages, bonuses and other benefits for
WSC staff. A 4% annual increase in constant prices has been added to pay levels.
Other costs: Projected expenses are increased in proportion to production capacity,
plus 101 p.a. in constant terms from 1997 through 2001, and by inflation thereafter.
Depreciation: The calculation of 5.15% has been made on the weighted average of all
fixed assets in operation through to 2001, and by 2.43t thereafter.
Balance sheet
14.   Fixed assets: Include network, treatment plants (including land), with the
addition of plant and equipment when new and rehabilitated assets are placed in
service, and are revalued at annual projected inflation rates. Accounts receivable:
Based on past experience, these have been assumed to equal 49 days' sales in 1996,
reducing to 46 days' sales in 2004. Inventories: These have been assumed to increase
in proportion to additional net fixed assets in service. Accounts payable:
Historical figures have been projected to increase in line with operational
expenses.
Includes also water supply systems (enterprises) in Uong Bi and Mao Khe which are not benefiting from
the project.

Source and application of funds
15.   Other capital contributions: Actual and projected contributions by DANIDA to
support the WSC through project supervision, trainers and advisors; other additions
consist of equity contributions by the Government equal to the amount of interest
during construction included in the cost of the project; plus an equity contribution
from the Provincial PC.  Loans: The IDA US$12.6 million credit and Danish grant
US$5.0 million (VND 193.8 billion) are assumed to be on-lent to the WSC by the
Government over 20 years, with a five year grace period, at an interest rate of 6.5%
p.a. A Danish contribution of US$3.1 million (VND 33.7 billion) is assumed to be
on-lent on the same terms and conditions as the IDA credit. Another loan to help
fund the follow-up second water supply project on the same terms and conditions as
the first loan is assumed to commence in 2004.
16.   Interest during construction: Capitalized interest charged at 6.5% p.a. on the
on-lent IDA (ITF) credit and the Danish grant and contribution from 1997 through
2001 for the first project, and from 2002 to 2006 for the follow-up second project.

38.9
DANANG COMPONENT
Income statement
17.   Revenues:  Water revenues  have  been projected  to  increase  in line with
estimated increased water supply, and annual increases of water tariffs. Water
supply is projected to increase by about 5% p.a. from 1996 through 2000, partly as
a result of the French Government financed network upgrading project, and by about
34% in 2001 and 69% in 2002 following the completion of the Cam Dai treatment plant
at the end of 2001. NRW is projected to remain at 30% from 1996 through 2004.
Average water tariffs are assumed to increase by 18% in 1996, 10% p.a. from 1997 to
2000, 15% in 2001, and 20% thereafter.
18.   Operational costs: Staff costs: Include wages, bonuses and other benefits for
WBC staff. A 4% annual increase in constant prices has been added to pay levels.
Other costs: Projected expenses are increased in proportion to additional production
capacity. Depreciation: The calculation of 5.65% p.a. has been made on the weighted
average of all fixed assets in operation.
Balance sheet
19.   Fixed assets: Include network, treatment plants (including land), with the
addition of plant and equipment when new assets are placed in service, and are



130                         ANNEX 10
revalued at annual projected inflation rates. Accounts receivable: Based on past
experience, these have been assumed to reduce from 57 days in 1996 to 42 days' sales
by 2004. Inventories: These have been assumed to increase in proportion to
additional net fixed assets in service. Accounts payable: Historical figures have
been projected to increase in line with operational expenses.
Source and application of funds
20.   Other  capital  contributions:  Actual  and projected  contributions  by  the
Australian Government to support the WSC through trainers and advisors; other
additions consist of equity contributions by the Government equal to the amount of
interest during construction included in the cost of the project; and municipal
equity of VND 45 billion. Loans: The IDA US$33.8 million (VND 372.0 billion) credit
is assumed to be on-lent to the WSC by the Government over 20 years, with a five
year grace period, at interest rate of 6.5% p.a.
21.   Interest during construction: Capitalized interest charged at 6.5% p.a. on the
on-lent IDA (ITF) credit from 1997 through 2001.

WATER SUPPLY PROJECT
Project performance monitoring
1.          The Monitoring and Evaluation  (M&E)  system is designed to. provide
managers with information on progress towards project objectives, impact on
beneficiaries, and institutional, technical and financial aspects that could be
useful in the commercial operation of the water supply companies. Three basic
components would be proposed for the M&E system:
a)    Performance Agreements between the PCs and WSCs;
b)    Public Performance Audits (PPAs) of WSCs by an independent agency; and
c)    More traditional tracking of project milestones in terms of measuring
progress achieved against specific targets in project implementation
plans.
Performance Agreements
2.          Performance Agreements (PA) would be intended to provide incentives for
the management of WSCs which are state enterprises to improve performance. The
criteria, their base values and annual targets and weights, and the evaluation
methodology would be agreed between the PCs and the management of WSCs at the
beginning of each year. The PA would be closely linked to the Corporate Plan of the
WSC. Bonus payments would be linked to performance measured against the PA.
Performance Agreements introduced for state enterprises including WSCs in Thailand
would be used as the model to be adapted to the specific conditions in Vietnam.
Public Performance Audits
3.          An  independent  agency  would  collect  information  on  performance
indicators of WSCs and make comparative information available for public disclosure.
The information would include indicators most relevant to consumers such as water
quality, pressure, reliability, etc. A simple grading system based on color coding
(e.g., gold for good, green for acceptable, black for unacceptable) would make the
information easily comprehensible to consumers. Public disclosure of comparative
information would generate pressure to improve performance and competition amongst
the water supply companies.
Project Milestones
4.          Traditional milestones,  in addition to the above, would be used to
evaluate project progress by the supervision missions. A detailed list of indicators
is provided in Table A 11.1 while key performance indicators relevant during project
implementation, agreed upon during negotiations, are highlighted in Table A 11.3.
The key performance indicators were identified using the Performance/Risk Summary
shown in Table A 11.2.

139
ANNEX 12
VIETNAM
WATER SUPPLY PROJECT
Rate of return
Data
1.    Data for the "without project" scenario is taken from the WSCs' income statements
in Annex 9. The base year is taken to be 1995, the last full year for which complete
accounts are available. Data on water produced, percentage of water billed and average
tariff are used to compute gross revenues. Operating expenses are adjusted by deleting
the item for non-collected bills which is not an expense and the item for connection
charges which would be financed out of the capital budget. For purposes of the rate of
return computation, the "without project" scenario assumes the 1995 values to remain
constant in real terms except for operating expenses which are assumed to increase in
real terms by 0.5% per year due to system deterioration. The base values are shown in
Table A 12.1.
2.    For the "with project" scenario, Table A 12.2 shows the project investment costs
(from Annex 3), excluding price contingencies, and the phasing of annual investment used
in the analysis. Operating costs are also taken from Annex 9 and projected using 1995
unit costs for the various cost categories, except staff costs, and multiplying them by
the amount of water produced in each year. Thus no efficiency gains or economy of scale
factors are built in. Staff costs are projected to increase at 4% per year in real terms
reflecting rising real income levels in Vietnam. Both investment costs and operating
costs are in constant 1995 values.
3.    No additional water is assumed to be available till 2000. However, non-revenue
water is projected to begin decreasing earlier as technical assistance focused on
improved billing and collection will be completed prior to the project becoming
effective. This is reasonable since administrative losses greatly exceed physical losses
in WSCs in Vietnam. Tariffs are also assumed to increase from 1997 as this has been
agreed with the PPCs. The variables are assumed to reach steady state in 2004.
Assumptions
4.    For the economic analysis, all costs are expressed in 1995 prices, making no
adjustments for shadow exchange rate or shadow labor costs in line with the assumption
made in Power sector projects in Vietnam. Electricity costs are not adjusted as the WSCs
are being charged 600 VND per kWh which is the long run marginal cost of supply at the
high voltage level. Staff and electricity costs comprise the bulk of operating costs.
There is some evidence that prices of chemicals are subsidized to the WSCs. However,
these are less than 10% of total operating costs and are not adjusted. Rather, any
likely impact is evaluated through sensitivity analysis on total operating costs. The
sensitivity results indicate that it is not worthwhile to make adjustments for the
distortion in the price of chemicals. Household size is taken to be 4.5 in each city.
Results
5.    Tables A 12.3, A 12.4 and A 12.5 show the data used, the computations and the
sensitivity analysis for the FIRR. Tables A 12.6, A 12.7 and A 12.8 are the
corresponding tables for the EIRR.
